Town Board Regular Meeting Minutes  
Wednesday, May 20, 2026 – 6:00 PM 
 
I.  Call to Order 
The meeting was called to order by Supervisor Halpin at 6:05 PM 
II.  Notice 
 ● Notice with Zoom Credentials  
III.  Invocation - Kathleen Berezny, Chaplain of the Ladies Auxiliary for the 
Riverhead Fire Department 
Invocation given 
IV.  Announcements 
Troop 94 was recognized for their contribution to the Town. 
Council member Merrifield reminded the community of the CAP (Community 
Awareness Program) that is having a Take Back Medicine day on May 30th at the 
Highway Department on Osborne Ave. Asking residents to empty out old and 
expired medication and drop off for proper destruction, no questions asked. 
Also reminded the community that the CAP March, where 5th and 6th grade 
students celebrate tolerance to Just say No, to drugs and peer pressure, will be 
held on June 5th. 
On June 16th, the Town Board will be honoring 16 seniors who are graduating who 
have dedicated their time to the goals of CAP. 
V.  Acknowledgement of Scouts from Wading River Troop 94, Working to 
Complete Their Citizenship in the Community Merit Badge 
Scouts were honored and given certificates by the board

VIII.  Public Hearings 
 ● 6:00 PM Public Hearing - 111 East Main St - Eminent Domain  
The Public Hearing opened at 6:14 pm. Frank Isler Esq, gave an overview and 
foundation for the purpose of the hearing. 
Dawn Thomas via Zoom attended and gave the history of the parcel and the long-
term plan for the main street area.  
Jeffrey Seaman, an environmental consultant for the East Main Street renewal 
plan.  
Cindy Clifford, Laura Jens Smith, Gail Walleck, Member of Council Rothwell, Mike 
Dubois, Garrett Moore via Letter, Council member Waski, Taque Terchin, Ron 
Harari via Zoom, Joan Cear, Jimmy Carasano, Collin Tooker, John McAuliff, 
Claudette Bianco, Kevin Shea, Peter Timmons, James Wooten, Denise Civiletti, 
Merrideth McDonald, Allyson Mattway via Zoom all participated.  
The meeting was closed. Will be left open for written comment for 10 days.  
Transcripts will be available upon request provided by Flynn Transcription 
services.   
 ● 6:00 PM- Public Hearing- Amend Chapter 301, Art XVII, Business F  
Greg Bergman gave an overview of the amendment to the chapter.  
Laura Jens Smith questioned whether height will create additional offices or retail 
on the second floor, and drive-through restaurants will compete with existing cr 58 
businesses.  
Martin Sendlewski passed up the recommendation for the site plan at the Tanger 
outlet. Closed 9:06. Held open for 10 days open for written comments 
 ● 6:05 PM- Public Hearing-Amend Chapter 301,Part 3, Supplementary 
Regulations  
The Public Hearing opened at 9:08 pm. TA Erik Howard gave an overview of the 
amendment. 
Taque Turchin asked if this proposal is retroactive or only going forward to new 
applications.  
Closed 9:18 pm. Held open for10 days for written comments 
 ● 6:10 PM Public Hearing- Amend Chapter 293- Shellfish and Finfish  
TA Erik Howard gave an overview of the proposed amendment. 
No comments closed at 9:20pm. Held open for written comments for 10 days 
 ● 6:10 PM- Public Hearing-Amend Chapter 231, Art IV-Fire Prevention  
TA Erik Howard gave an overview of the proposed amendment. No Comments. 
Closed 9:22, Held open for written comments for10 days 
IX.  Comments on Resolutions 
Taque Turchin-  questioned resolution 523 with a settlement of legal action for a 
prior claim. 
Resolution 520 YMCA — Debbie Nightall spoke in favor of the benefits of a YMCA 
within Riverhead 
Resolution 501-June 10 special meeting.—John McAuliff questioned if the public 
could alter the path of the proposal in place for the Peconic Hotel at the public 
hearing 
Resolution 507-508 racetrack not street — Barbara Blass wanted to know about 
the temporary use permit and advertising into 2027and the advertising slogan 
using the Epcal Site.

2              SUPERVISOR HALPIN:  Good evening,
3           ladies and gentlemen, today is

6              ADMINISTRATOR THOMAS:  Hello,
7           everyone, can you here me?
8              COUNCILWOMAN MERRIFIELD:  Yes.
9              ADMINISTRATOR THOMAS:  Okay,
10           great.  The Town of Riverhead has
11           been actively attempting to
12           revitalize downtown for over
13           30 years.  This process began in
14           earnest in 1993 when the Town Board
15           designated East Main Street pursuant
16           to Article 15 of the New York State
17           General Municipal Law as an Urban
18           Renewable Area, a designation that
19           provides a host of revitalization
20           tools intended to facilitate the
21           removal of blighted and
22           underutilized buildings and to
23           facilitate development and
24           reinvestment.
25             These tools include -- oops,
Page 5
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           sorry -- ways to address blight and
3           deterioration, promoting clearance
4           replanting, reconstruction and
5           redevelopment and to foster
6           public/private partnerships in
7           bringing projects and development
8           that will improve these areas.
9             The plan gave the Town the power
10           to plan, undertake and management
11           urban renewal projects and to use
12           powers for public use essential for
13           public interest for which public
14           funds may be expended.
15             Since 1993, there have been more
16           than 20 formal revitalization plans
17           intended to ignite economic vitality
18           in our downtown.  Each of these
19           plans had its own purpose, but many
20           reach the same conclusions about the
21           elements and concepts needed to make
22           our downtown a thriving place in the
23           community.
24             These plans include the 1993 Urban
25           Renewal Plan, it's 2008 update.  The
Page 6
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           2016 Brownfield Opportunity Area
3           Study with its creative placemaking
4           supplement to name a few.  All were
5           intended to make our East Main
6           Street area vibrant -- the vibrant,
7           activated local business district we
8           all know it can be.
9             All of these studies were
10           completed with public engagement
11           including many public meetings,
12           surveys, polls, websites, workshops
13           where members of the public were
14           able to express their visions of the
15           downtown that they wanted to see.
16             Time and time again the idea of
17           connecting Main Street to the river
18           and preventing flooding were
19           identified as top priorities.  The
20           public continually and consistently
21           express desire to create an
22           activated public space with open
23           views of the river where they could
24           visit at playground, attend an
25           event, exercise, walk a dog, shop,
Page 7
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           spend time with friends, dine
3           outdoors, and generally enjoy our
4           historic downtown the way we all
5           know it can be.  In other words, the
6           downtown should be a place for
7           everyone.  The ultimate public
8           purpose.
9             In 2018, the Town finally got a
10           real foothold into implementing this
11           long-expressed desire to open up
12           Main Street to the Riverfront
13           through the creation of new public
14           place, a Town Square connecting to
15           Main Street to Heidi Behr Way with a
16           grant from New York State for
17           $800,000.
18             Since that time, the Town has
19           invested literally thousands of
20           hours advancing the Town Square
21           Project; acquiring properties;
22           removing blighted, vacant and
23           underutilized buildings; creating a
24           temporary public space; engaging in
25           public/private partnerships;
Page 8
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           designing the details of all of its
3           components and obtaining more than
4           $40 million in funding for the
5           various projects to the point where
6           we should be, within just a few
7           weeks, issuing building permits for
8           its construction.
9             The Town Square Project is, at
10           its very essence, a public purpose.
11           Consistent with the Urban Renewal
12           Plan in 1993, it will remove blight,
13           vacancy and deterioration from the
14           heart of our Downtown and provide
15           new public spaces for residents and
16           visitors and economic development
17           that will reutilize and support the
18           long term economic and physical
19           health of the Riverhead community
20           through public/private partnership.
21             The Town Square is intended to
22           become a focal point of public
23           activation in Downtown.  Its
24           components include an adaptive
25           playground, a splash pad and public
Page 9
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           event space for large and small
3           events of all kinds, a veterans
4           memorial space, a water feature,
5           places to dine outdoors, hold an
6           exercise class, art show, musical
7           performances and provide a gathering
8           space for special holiday events.
9           It's a place we could all be proud
10           of and enjoy.
11             The Town Square Project has
12           benefited from financial support and
13           government partnership through New
14           York State Downtown Revitalization
15           Initiative, New York State Empire
16           State Development, New York State
17           Historic Preservation Office and
18           Suffolk County and has received the
19           assistance of the U.S. Army Corps of
20           Engineers, particularly for flood
21           mitigation analysis and plans.
22             The Long Island Regional Economic
23           Development Council found it to be a
24           project of regional significance in
25           2021.  The project also involves a
Page 10
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           public/private partnership that will
3           activate the east side of the Town
4           Square with a new $30 million Hilton
5           Tapestry Hotel whose first floor
6           will provide retail space, food and
7           beverage -- and food and beverage
8           offerings adjacent to the Town
9           Square's public space while
10           providing needed hotel rooms for all
11           of the East End.
12             The activation plan created by --
13           in 2022 by Phil Myrick, the CEO --
14           former CEO of the Project for Public
15           Spaces who was engaged by the Town,
16           emphasized that in order to be
17           successful, all surrounding ground
18           floor uses in the Town Square should
19           reinforce the theme of family
20           entertainment; local, unique retail
21           and arts and culture.  All of the
22           Town Square renderings and public
23           engagement sessions envision both
24           sides of the Town Square providing
25           this essential activation and
Page 11
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           generating foot traffic throughout
3           downtown.
4             In 2021, the Town of Riverhead
5           purchased, and ultimately removed,
6           three vacant underutilized and/or
7           derelict buildings; 117, 121, and
8           127 East Main Street to begin
9           building the Town Square project.
10           These properties are now the
11           temporary grassy area directly
12           across from The Suffolk and the
13           location for the private hotel
14           developments that's to come.
15             The entire length of the former
16           Sweezy Department Store at 111 East
17           Main Street, which sits along the
18           west side of the Town Square has
19           been vacant, deteriorated,
20           substandard and blighted for well
21           over 20 years.  Nothing has been
22           done to improve its appearance, odor
23           or rotting facade.  That property
24           was purchased by its current owner
25           seven years ago -- approximately
Page 12
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           seven years ago.
3             In 2020, the owner proposed a
4           large redevelopment of the property
5           including a second floor planetarium.
6           The plan also included a first floor,
7           2,400-square foot restaurant; the
8           MakerSpace Gallery of 400 square
9           foot, a gift shop of 800 square foot
10           and its main entrance all facing the
11           Town Square.
12             This project proposed the
13           investment of $13.5 million and the
14           owner represented that the project
15           was intended to, consistent with the
16           Town's Downtown Activation Plan,
17           "Open up the solid wall facing east
18           and commercial space within the
19           existing footprint while activating
20           and enhancing the new Town Square."
21             Over the last seven years, the
22           Town's projects have moved ahead and
23           are now ready to begin.  As I
24           mentioned earlier, it took thousands
25           of hours of time to get to this
Page 13
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           point.  The Town hired consultants
3           including landscape architects,
4           environmental consultants, flood
5           mitigation engineers, surveyors,
6           architects, engineers and economic
7           consultants to help conceptualize
8           and finalize designs and ultimately
9           create construction drawings for
10           these projects.
11             The Town also developed a
12           partnership with a private developer
13           for the creation of a hotel, a $30
14           million private investment into the
15           project, which was recommended in
16           the market study that the Town
17           commissioned in 2022 as part of the
18           Reactivation Plan and is supported
19           by Urban Renewal Law.
20             Plans for drainage, sewer, water,
21           electric, landscaping, play
22           equipment, hotel interface, fire
23           access, cameras, lighting, internet
24           access, accessibility, flood
25           mitigation and water features all
Page 14
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           progress to completion and are now
3           in the process of being permitted
4           for construction as I mentioned
5           earlier.
6             Around this time last year it
7           became clear that after six years of
8           the original 24,000-square foot
9           project proposed by the owner of 111
10           East Main Street was not moving
11           forward.  As a result and due to the
12           owner's failure to move forward with
13           the activated needed on the --
14           activation needed on the Town
15           Square, in April of 2025, the Town
16           Board began eminent domain
17           proceedings to acquire the building
18           for public use.
19             On April 10th at a Town Board
20           Work Session, the representatives of
21           the property owner appeared before
22           the Town Board requesting that the
23           proceeding be suspended and that the
24           entity be permitted to advance a
25           substantially smaller version of the
Page 15
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           project, about half of what was
3           originally planned and represented
4           that the project would be completed
5           as originally planned, but in phases
6           albeit without a specific timeframe.
7             The representatives gave repeated
8           assurances that the plan's first
9           phases would be completed with the
10           east side prepared for the necessary
11           openings and eventual entrance onto
12           the Town Square and that the
13           structure would be modified so that
14           it was prepared for an eventual
15           second story to support planned
16           planetarium.  The representatives
17           promised an August 2025 grand
18           opening for the first phase.
19             The Town Board agreed and provided
20           the owner the time requested,
21           however, following the -- for the
22           following entire year, the building
23           remained vacant and blighted.  In
24           April of 2026, the Town Board,
25           seeking an update, requested the
Page 16
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           group back to explain its lack of
3           progress.
4             Instead of providing an update,
5           the representatives advanced an even
6           smaller plan for the project, now
7           80 percent smaller than the original
8           plan, leaving the entire east side
9           of the building as a blank wall and
10           renovating only the front half of
11           the first floor and the front of the
12           building.  No timeframe was provided
13           for any future phrases -- phases or
14           the plan to activate the Town Square
15           as promised.
16             What came to light at that
17           meeting and through further research
18           was that the entity was experiencing
19           financial difficulties and could not
20           promise that the funding was
21           available to complete the 20 percent
22           reduced sized project.  It was also
23           learned that the owners had a
24           $1.1 million mortgage and a
25           mechanics lien of $13,500.
Page 17
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           Representatives described the entity
3           at that time as a vulnerable
4           not-for-profit.
5             The plans are no longer in line
6           with the need for activation on the
7           Town Square.  The property in an
8           essential component and is key to
9           the long term success of the overall
10           Town Square Project, as expressed in
11           the many plans and by the members of
12           the public that participated in
13           those plans for over the last seven
14           years.
15             The vacant, blighted and
16           deteriorated building at 111 East
17           Main Street remains in the same
18           dilapidated condition that it was in
19           2019 in the heart of our downtown.
20           The owner recently sought to move
21           forward with the much smaller plan,
22           the minor interior fit-out and a
23           facade improvement, but, again, the
24           timeframe for the long term
25           activation plan was not specified or
Page 18
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           identified.
3             Longstanding planning principles
4           require successful public spaces to
5           be activated.  Allowing a brick wall
6           to exist on the entire west side of
7           the Town Square will prevent the
8           activation necessary for the success
9           of this major public project.
10           Moreover, the existence of this
11           long, blighted, vacant dilapidated
12           eyesore to remain in the center of
13           our Main Street Business District
14           does more than prevent the
15           activation we need, it actually
16           repels people.
17             The Town Square is a creative
18           placemaking project with a strong
19           public purpose.  It is intended to
20           attract people to it for activities,
21           offerings, events, performances,
22           markets, relaxation and there's a
23           connection to the Peconic River that
24           hasn't ever existed.
25             As our consultant, Phil Myrick,
Page 19
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           expressed, both sides of the Town
3           Square need to be activated in this
4           way to fulfill the public purpose of
5           Town Square Project.  A blank, brick
6           wall running along the entire west
7           side will make it difficult for the
8           Town Square Project to be
9           successful.  The opportunity for a
10           successful Town Square Project hinges
11           on activation and the current owner's
12           plans provides none.
13             The Town is on the precipice of
14           meaningful revitalization after
15           waiting for over 30 years while the
16           redevelopment concept proposed by
17           the owner of 111 East Main Street,
18           provided in 2020, with the plan
19           24,000 square foot and $13.5 million
20           investment might have fulfilled
21           activation necessary for the Town
22           Square to fulfill its public
23           purpose, the current plan actually
24           hinders it.
25             Ensuring that the millions of
Page 20
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           dollars in public investment in this
3           public project is protected and due

5           of Downtown and directly on the Town

10           recommending the acquisition of the
11           building to ensure that what is

13           maximizes the public purpose of the
14           Town Square's being created to

17              MR. SEAMAN:  Thank you for the
18           question because I think it will
19           shed some clarity on both the
20           municipal and public importance that
21           you have under your consideration.
22           And I think to restate Councilwoman
23           Waski's concerns, this is not an
24           argument about a Science Center.  It
25           is about a parcel of land with a
Page 90
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           blighted building.
3             What is critical in the Phase 1
4           of the Downtown Revitalization
5           Program is the integration of all of
6           the properties on the south side of
7           Main Street.  Those properties that
8           face the river and have been subject
9           to almost catastrophic flooding
10           caused by significant nor'easters,
11           especially when those storms come in
12           with large amounts of precipitation.
13             They generally occur,
14           historically, in March and in
15           October and unfortunately for flood
16           victims, that's also when the
17           groundwater is at its highest
18           elevations.  So with all the
19           impervious surface that's part of
20           all of Main Street, there's just no
21           place for the water to go until it
22           hits the parking lot, which I think
23           has been studied by not only the
24           Army Corps of Engineers, but
25           experienced by many of the business
Page 91
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           owners, property owners, the public
3           and the Town.
4             So as part of the plan, East End
5           Arts Center property will be
6           elevated, they're buildings
7           relocated, to get them out of the
8           flood zone.  The proposed hotel site
9           plan clearly indicates that they're
10           both storm water and elevations of
11           the building and all the other
12           infrastructure that are being
13           incorporated into that plan are also
14           addressing the flood mitigation by
15           removing those structures out of the
16           flood zone and providing adequate
17           infrastructure to control surface
18           generated runoff.  Not only of their
19           project, but other interrelated
20           projects.
21             We come to the Town Square and
22           the design engineers came up with a
23           stepped design, meaning the
24           elevations will change from Main
25           Street, which is at about 13 and
Page 92
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           14 feet above mean sea level, down
3           to Heidi Behr Way.  That integration
4           of all these parcels are all part of
5           the flood mitigation program.  One
6           parcel would cause the other parcels
7           to continue to flood unless they're
8           all systemically raised and the
9           infrastructure provided in order
10           address this mass flooding issue.
11             Without the information from
12           111 East Main Street, we have no
13           idea of how they would be integrated
14           into our flood mitigation program
15           without seeing some real hard
16           information, engineering details on
17           the building elevations, engineering
18           details on how their storm water
19           system would integrate with others.
20             As the parcel stays today, if all
21           other development took place and
22           that was not integrated now or soon
23           into the future, that building would
24           flood.  That would be the low point
25           in the flood mitigation program.
Page 93
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           That would impact that property
3           owner unfairly.  The only potential
4           opportunity would be to construct a
5           retaining wall that would isolate
6           that building.
7             It might still flood based on
8           other storm water runoff or storm
9           conditions that take place, but the
10           real public purpose here is to
11           finalize that integration for the
12           flood mitigation program.  That is
13           the single driving force behind the
14           social and economic benefits of
15           whatever else takes place in Downtown.
16             We didn't predict in the earlier
17           studies what would take place on
18           this parcel if it is acquired.  All

20           had done in order to determine a use

22           were identified as a key market
23           study component, and apply that in a
24           theoretical manner to that parcel at
25           111 so that I could figure out,
Page 94
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           potentially, how much water would be

23             To plant a Town Square is noble

Page 141
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           dirt and a river just flows without
3           the deep roots where community

6           in sun, the Science Center's quite
7           work has been done.  375,000 seeds,
8           the minds of our children, their
9           hopes and their needs have been
10           watered and nurtured to help them
11           look high from the soil of Riverhead
12           up to the sky.
13             And it is not just the blossom of
14           youth that will gather, but the
15           shade of the old trees enjoying the
16           weather where retirees mentor the
17           young who pass through a space for
18           the lifetime to gather and renew.
19             In 2020 they bought their own
20           ground, 111 Main Street structurally
21           sound.  They crowned it with armor
22           against winter rains, a brand new
23           roof paid by their own careful
24           gains.  And this Town called this
25           center a deep water anchor to draw
Page 142
1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           in the funding without any ranker.
3             We use this bright vision of
4           science and grace to harvest 10
5           million from the State for this
6           place.  But you cannot grow forest
7           by chopping the root and you cannot
8           expect a dead orchard to fruit.
9             You claim there's no progress,
10           that reports were not made, but the
11           roots were communicating deep with
12           the shade.  The Planning Department
13           received every sheet, but it died on
14           the vine before reaching your seat.

1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
2           sky.  Why punish the nonprofit
3           steady and true for the very same

1     Riverhead Planning Board  ~ May 20, 2026
